<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Axl Rose</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>W. Axl Rose</b> (born <b>William Bruce Rose Jr.</b>; raised as <b>William Bruce Bailey</b>; February 6, 1962)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> is an American singer, songwriter, record producer and musician. He is the lead vocalist of the <a href="/wiki/Hard_rock" title="Hard rock">hard rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a>, a position he has held since its inception in 1985. In addition to Guns N' Roses, he is also the current lead singer of <a href="/wiki/AC/DC" title="AC/DC">AC/DC</a> since 2016. Due to his powerful and wide vocal range and energetic live performances, Rose has been named one of the greatest singers of all time by various media outlets, including <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Lafayette,_Indiana" title="Lafayette, Indiana">Lafayette, Indiana</a>, Rose moved to Los Angeles in the early 1980s, where he became active in the local hard rock scene and joined several bands, including <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Rose" title="Hollywood Rose">Hollywood Rose</a> and <a href="/wiki/L.A._Guns" title="L.A. Guns">L.A. Guns</a>. In 1985, he co-founded Guns N' Roses, with whom he had great success and recognition in the late 1980s and early 1990s. Their first album, <i><a href="/wiki/Appetite_for_Destruction" title="Appetite for Destruction">Appetite for Destruction</a></i> (1987), has sold in excess of 30 million copies worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Havelock_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Havelock-8">[8]</a></sup> and is one of the best-selling debut albums of all time in the U.S. with 18 million units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-9">[9]</a></sup> Its full-length follow-ups, the twin albums <i><a href="/wiki/Use_Your_Illusion_I" title="Use Your Illusion I">Use Your Illusion I</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Use_Your_Illusion_II" title="Use Your Illusion II">Use Your Illusion II</a></i> (1991), were also widely successful; they respectively debuted at No. 2 and No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and have sold a combined 35 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>After 1994, following the conclusion of their two-and-a-half-year <a href="/wiki/Use_Your_Illusion_Tour" title="Use Your Illusion Tour">Use Your Illusion Tour</a>, Rose disappeared from public life for several years, while the band disintegrated due to personal and musical differences. As its sole remaining original member, he was able to continue working under the Guns N' Roses banner because he had legally obtained the band name. In 2001, he resurfaced with a new line-up of Guns N' Roses at <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio#Rock_in_Rio_3" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio 3</a>, and subsequently played periodic concert tours to promote the long-delayed <i><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Democracy" title="Chinese Democracy">Chinese Democracy</a></i> (2008), which undersold the music industry's commercial expectations despite positive reviews upon its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllMusic_Biography_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic_Biography-11">[11]</a></sup> In 2012, Rose was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> as a member of Guns N' Roses, though he declined to attend the event and requested exclusion from the HoF. In 2016, Rose partially reunited the 'classic' lineup of Guns N' Roses and toured the world as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Not_In_This_Lifetime..._Tour" title="Not In This Lifetime... Tour">Not In This Lifetime... Tour</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Axl_child.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="185" data-file-width="200" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/84/Axl_child.jpg" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Axl_child.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rose as a child.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Axl Rose was born William Bruce Rose, Jr. in <a href="/wiki/Lafayette,_Indiana" title="Lafayette, Indiana">Lafayette, Indiana</a>, the oldest child of Sharon Elizabeth (née Lintner), then 16 years old and still in high school,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-watchyoubleed_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-watchyoubleed-12">[12]</a></sup> and William Bruce Rose, then 20 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reitwiesner_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reitwiesner-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStoneBio_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStoneBio-14">[14]</a></sup> His father has been described as "a troubled and charismatic local delinquent," and the pregnancy was unplanned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-watchyoubleed_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-watchyoubleed-12">[12]</a></sup> His parents separated when Rose was approximately two years old, prompting his father to abduct and allegedly <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">molest</a> him before disappearing from Lafayette.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-watchyoubleed_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-watchyoubleed-12">[12]</a></sup> His mother remarried to Stephen L. Bailey, and changed her son's name to William Bruce Bailey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStoneBio_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStoneBio-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tannenbaum88_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tannenbaum88-15">[15]</a></sup> He has two younger siblings—a sister, Amy, and a half-brother, Stuart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStone00_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStone00-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wall07_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wall07-17">[17]</a></sup> Until the age of 17, Rose believed that Bailey was his natural father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely92_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neely92-18">[18]</a></sup> He never met his biological father as an adult; William Rose, Sr. was murdered in <a href="/wiki/Marion,_Illinois" title="Marion, Illinois">Marion, Illinois</a>, in 1984 by a criminal acquaintance who was convicted even though the body was never recovered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Rose did not learn about the murder until years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wall90_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wall90-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Bailey household was very religious; Rose and his family attended a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> church, where he was required to attend services three to eight times per week and even taught <a href="/wiki/Sunday_school" title="Sunday school">Sunday school</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James92_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-James92-21">[21]</a></sup> Rose later recalled an oppressive upbringing, stating, "We'd have televisions one week, then my stepdad would throw them out because they were Satanic. I wasn't allowed to listen to music. Women were evil. Everything was evil."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James92_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-James92-21">[21]</a></sup> He accused his stepfather of physically abusing him and his siblings and sexually abusing his sister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStoneBio_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStoneBio-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely92_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Neely92-18">[18]</a></sup> Rose found solace in music from an early age. He sang in the church choir from the age of five, and performed at services with his brother and sister under the name the Bailey Trio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTVRockumentary_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTVRockumentary-22">[22]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_High_School_(Indiana)" title="Jefferson High School (Indiana)">Jefferson High School</a>, he participated in the school chorus and studied piano.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James89_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-James89-23">[23]</a></sup> A second baritone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Superteen89_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Superteen89-24">[24]</a></sup> Rose began developing "different voices" during chorus practice to confuse his teacher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTVRockumentary_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-MTVRockumentary-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Superteen89_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Superteen89-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> He eventually formed a band with his friends, one of whom was Jeff Isbell, later known as <a href="/wiki/Izzy_Stradlin" title="Izzy Stradlin">Izzy Stradlin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geffen98_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Geffen98-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the age of 17, while going through insurance papers in his parents' home, Rose learned of his biological father's existence, and he unofficially readopted his birth name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tannenbaum88_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tannenbaum88-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely92_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-Neely92-18">[18]</a></sup> However, he referred to himself only as W. Rose, because he did not want to share a first name with his biological father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tannenbaum88_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tannenbaum88-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely92_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-Neely92-18">[18]</a></sup> Following the discovery of his true family origins, Rose became the local juvenile delinquent in Lafayette; he was arrested more than 20 times on charges such as public intoxication and battery, and served jail terms up to three months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tannenbaum88_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-Tannenbaum88-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kuipers91_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kuipers91-27">[27]</a></sup> After Lafayette authorities threatened to charge him as a habitual criminal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James89_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-James89-23">[23]</a></sup> Rose moved to Los Angeles, California, in December 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kuipers91_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kuipers91-27">[27]</a></sup> After moving to Los Angeles, he became so engrossed in his band AXL that his friends suggested he call himself Axl Rose;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tannenbaum88_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-Tannenbaum88-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> he legally changed his name to W. Axl Rose prior to signing his contract with <a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen Records</a> in March 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Superteen89_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-Superteen89-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kuipers91_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kuipers91-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sugerman91_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sugerman91-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1983.E2.80.9386:_Early_years">1983–86: Early years</span></h3>
<p>Shortly after his arrival in Los Angeles, Rose met guitarist Kevin Lawrence outside <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Troubadour_(Los_Angeles)" title="The Troubadour (Los Angeles)">The Troubadour</a> in West Hollywood and joined his band <a href="/wiki/Rapidfire" title="Rapidfire">Rapidfire</a>. They recorded a four-song demo in May 1983,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> which, after years of legal action, was released as an EP, <i>Ready to Rumble</i>, in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> After parting ways with Lawrence, he formed the band <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Rose" title="Hollywood Rose">Hollywood Rose</a> with his childhood friend Izzy Stradlin,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> who had moved to Los Angeles in 1980,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geffen98_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Geffen98-26">[26]</a></sup> and sixteen-year-old guitarist <a href="/wiki/Chris_Weber" title="Chris Weber">Chris Weber</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-L.A._Guns_AMG_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-L.A._Guns_AMG-35">[35]</a></sup> In January 1984, the band recorded a five-song demo featuring the tracks "Anything Goes", "Rocker", "Shadow of Your Love", and "Reckless Life", which was released in 2004 as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Roots_of_Guns_N%27_Roses" title="The Roots of Guns N' Roses">The Roots of Guns N' Roses</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Guitarist <a href="/wiki/Slash_(musician)" title="Slash (musician)">Slash</a> and drummer <a href="/wiki/Steven_Adler" title="Steven Adler">Steven Adler</a>, future members of <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a>, joined Hollywood Rose before the band's dissolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slash_84_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slash_84-37">[37]</a></sup> Rose then joined the first line-up of <a href="/wiki/L.A._Guns" title="L.A. Guns">L.A. Guns</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> While struggling to make an impact on the Hollywood music scene, Rose held down a variety of jobs, including the position of night manager at the <a href="/wiki/Tower_Records" title="Tower Records">Tower Records</a> location on <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Boulevard" title="Sunset Boulevard">Sunset Boulevard</a>. Rose and Stradlin also smoked cigarettes for a scientific study at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA">UCLA</a> for the reported wages of $8 per hour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sugerman91_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sugerman91-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1985, Rose and his former band mate <a href="/wiki/Tracii_Guns" title="Tracii Guns">Tracii Guns</a> formed Guns N' Roses by merging their respective bands Hollywood Rose and L.A. Guns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spitz99_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spitz99-39">[39]</a></sup> By June, after several line-up changes, the band consisted of Rose, lead guitarist Slash, rhythm guitarist Izzy Stradlin, bassist <a href="/wiki/Duff_McKagan" title="Duff McKagan">Duff McKagan</a>, and drummer Steven Adler. The line-up debuted at The Troubadour and proceeded to play the L.A. club circuit, eventually building a devoted fan following.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spitz99_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Spitz99-39">[39]</a></sup> The band attracted the attention of several major record labels,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spitz99_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-Spitz99-39">[39]</a></sup> before signing with Geffen Records in March 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James89_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-James89-23">[23]</a></sup> The following December, they released the four-song EP <i><a href="/wiki/Live_%3F!*@_Like_a_Suicide" title="Live ?!*@ Like a Suicide">Live ?!*@ Like a Suicide</a></i> on the Geffen imprint <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UZI_Suicide" title="UZI Suicide">UZI Suicide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStoneBio_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStoneBio-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1987.E2.80.9389:_Breakthrough_with_Appetite_for_Destruction">1987–89: Breakthrough with <i>Appetite for Destruction</i></span></h3>
<p>In July 1987, Guns N' Roses released its debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Appetite_for_Destruction" title="Appetite for Destruction">Appetite for Destruction</a></i>. Although the record received critical acclaim, it experienced a modest commercial start, selling as many as 500,000 copies in its first year of release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wiggins03_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wiggins03-40">[40]</a></sup> However, fueled by the band's relentless touring and the mainstream success of the single "<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Child_o%27_Mine" title="Sweet Child o' Mine">Sweet Child o' Mine</a>"—Rose's tribute to his then-girlfriend Erin Everly—the album rose to the No. 1 position on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> in August 1988, and again in February 1989. To date, <i>Appetite for Destruction</i> has sold over 30 million copies worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Havelock_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Havelock-8">[8]</a></sup> 18 million of which sold in the United States, making it the best-selling debut album of all time in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the band's performance at the <a href="/wiki/Monsters_of_Rock" title="Monsters of Rock">Monsters of Rock</a> festival in <a href="/wiki/Castle_Donington" title="Castle Donington">Castle Donington</a>, England, in August 1988, two fans were crushed to death when many in the crowd of 107,000 began slam-dancing to "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_So_Easy_(Guns_N%27_Roses_song)" title="It's So Easy (Guns N' Roses song)">It's So Easy</a>". Rose had halted the show several times to calm the audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tannenbaum88_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-Tannenbaum88-15">[15]</a></sup> From then on, he became known for personally addressing disruptive fans and giving instructions to security personnel from the stage, at times stopping concerts to deal with issues in the crowd. In 1992, Rose stated, "Most performers would go to a security person in their organization, and it would just be done very quietly. I'll confront the person, stop the song: 'Guess what: You wasted your money, you get to leave.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely92_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-Neely92-18">[18]</a></sup> As a result of the deaths at Monsters of Rock, the festival was canceled the following year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 1988, Guns N' Roses released the stopgap album <i><a href="/wiki/G_N%27_R_Lies" title="G N' R Lies">G N' R Lies</a></i>, which sold more than five million copies in the U.S. alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-9">[9]</a></sup> The band – and Rose in particular – were accused of promoting racist and homophobic attitudes with the song "<a href="/wiki/One_in_a_Million_(Guns_N%27_Roses_song)" title="One in a Million (Guns N' Roses song)">One in a Million</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goldstein89_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goldstein89-42">[42]</a></sup> in which Rose warns "<a href="/wiki/Nigger" title="Nigger">niggers</a>" to "get out of my way" and complains about "<a href="/wiki/Faggot_(slang)" title="Faggot (slang)">faggots</a>" who "spread some fucking disease." During the controversy, Rose defended his use of the racial slur by claiming that "it's a word to describe somebody that is basically a pain in your life, a problem. The word nigger doesn't necessarily mean black."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James89_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-James89-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1992, however, he conceded that he had used the word as an insult towards black people, stating, "I was pissed off about some black people that were trying to rob me. I wanted to insult those particular black people. I didn't want to support racism."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely92_18-5"><a href="#cite_note-Neely92-18">[18]</a></sup> In response to the allegations of homophobia, Rose stated that he considered himself "pro-heterosexual" and blamed this attitude on "bad experiences" with gay men, citing an attempted rape in his late teens and the alleged molestation by his biological father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely92_18-6"><a href="#cite_note-Neely92-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James89_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-James89-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sischy92_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sischy92-43">[43]</a></sup> The controversy led to Guns N' Roses being dropped from the roster of an AIDS benefit show in New York organized by the <a href="/wiki/Gay_Men%27s_Health_Crisis" title="Gay Men's Health Crisis">Gay Men's Health Crisis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James89_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-James89-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sugerman91_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sugerman91-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the success of <i>Appetite for Destruction</i> and <i>G N' R Lies</i>, Rose found himself lauded as one of rock's most prominent frontmen. By the time he appeared solo on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> in August 1989, his celebrity was such that the influential music magazine agreed to his absolute requirement that the interview and accompanying photographs would be provided by two of his friends, writer <a href="/wiki/Del_James" title="Del James">Del James</a> and photographer <a href="/wiki/Robert_John_(photographer)" title="Robert John (photographer)">Robert John</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WAR_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-WAR-44">[44]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> anchorman <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Loder" title="Kurt Loder">Kurt Loder</a> described Rose as "maybe the finest hard rock singer currently on the scene, and certainly the most charismatic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Loder90_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Loder90-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990.E2.80.9393:_International_success_with_Use_Your_Illusion">1990–93: International success with <i>Use Your Illusion</i></span></h3>
<p>In early 1990, Guns N' Roses returned to the studio to begin recording the full-length follow-up to <i>Appetite for Destruction</i>. Recording sessions initially proved unproductive due to Steven Adler's struggle with drug addiction, which made him unable to perform and caused sessions to abort for several days at a time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spitz99_39-3"><a href="#cite_note-Spitz99-39">[39]</a></sup> Adler was fired the following July and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Matt_Sorum" title="Matt Sorum">Matt Sorum</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Cult" title="The Cult">The Cult</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spitz99_39-4"><a href="#cite_note-Spitz99-39">[39]</a></sup> Keyboardist <a href="/wiki/Dizzy_Reed" title="Dizzy Reed">Dizzy Reed</a> also joined the band that year at Rose's insistence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spitz99_39-5"><a href="#cite_note-Spitz99-39">[39]</a></sup> Sorum and Reed played their first show with Guns N' Roses at <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio#Rock_in_Rio_2" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio 2</a> in January 1991. The group fired its long-time manager, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Niven" title="Alan Niven">Alan Niven</a>, in May of that year; Rose reportedly forced the dismissal of Niven against the wishes of his band mates by refusing to complete the new album until Niven was gone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely91_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Neely91-46">[46]</a></sup> He was replaced by roadie Doug Goldstein, whom Izzy Stradlin described as "the guy who gets to go over to Axl's at six in the morning after he's smashed his $60,000 grand piano out of the picture window."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kent03_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kent03-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 1991, still without an album to promote, the band embarked on the two-and-a-half-year <a href="/wiki/Use_Your_Illusion_Tour" title="Use Your Illusion Tour">Use Your Illusion Tour</a>, which became known for its financial success and myriad controversial incidents that occurred during shows, including late starts, on-stage rantings and even riots. Rose received much criticism for his late appearances at concerts, sometimes taking the stage hours after the band was scheduled to perform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely92_18-7"><a href="#cite_note-Neely92-18">[18]</a></sup> In July 1991, 90 minutes into a concert at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverport_Amphitheater" title="Riverport Amphitheater">Riverport Amphitheater</a> near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis</a>, after on-stage requests from Rose for security personnel to confiscate a fan's video camera, Rose himself dived into the crowd to seize the contraband item. After being pulled back on stage, he announced, "Thanks to the lame-ass security, I'm going home!" and departed, following which some 2500 fans staged <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverport_riot" title="Riverport riot">a riot</a>, resulting in an estimated $200,000 in damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Axl_rose_in_israel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="364" data-file-width="346" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Axl_rose_in_israel.jpg/220px-Axl_rose_in_israel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Axl_rose_in_israel.jpg/330px-Axl_rose_in_israel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/98/Axl_rose_in_israel.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Axl_rose_in_israel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rose at <a href="/wiki/Yarkon_Park" title="Yarkon Park">Yarkon Park</a> in Tel Aviv, Israel, in May 1993</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In September 1991, with enough material completed for two albums, Guns N' Roses released <i><a href="/wiki/Use_Your_Illusion_I" title="Use Your Illusion I">Use Your Illusion I</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Use_Your_Illusion_II" title="Use Your Illusion II">Use Your Illusion II</a></i>, which debuted at No. 2 and No. 1 respectively on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, a feat not achieved by any other group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sugerman91_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sugerman91-29">[29]</a></sup> By the albums' release, however, Rose's relationships with his bandmates had become increasingly strained. His childhood friend Izzy Stradlin abruptly left the group in November 1991; he was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Gilby_Clarke" title="Gilby Clarke">Gilby Clarke</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kill_For_Thrills" title="Kill For Thrills">Kill For Thrills</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spitz99_39-6"><a href="#cite_note-Spitz99-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sischy92_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sischy92-43">[43]</a></sup> Of his reasons for leaving, Stradlin said, "I didn't like the complications that became such a part of daily life in Guns N' Roses,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Musician92_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Musician92-49">[49]</a></sup> citing the riot and Rose's chronic lateness as examples, as well as his new-found sobriety making it difficult to be around other bandmates continued alcohol and substance abuse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geffen98_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Geffen98-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Musician92_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Musician92-49">[49]</a></sup> At some point during the remainder of the tour, Rose reportedly demanded, and received, sole ownership of the Guns N' Roses name from Slash and Duff McKagan; Rose allegedly issued an ultimatum—they had to sign the name over to him or he would not perform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStone00_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStone00-16">[16]</a></sup> (In 2008, however, Rose stated that these reports were false and that the alleged coercion would have rendered the contract legally untenable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>)</p>
<p>Another riot occurred in August 1992 at Montreal's <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Montreal)" title="Olympic Stadium (Montreal)">Olympic Stadium</a>, during a <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses/Metallica_Stadium_Tour" title="Guns N' Roses/Metallica Stadium Tour">co-headlining tour</a> with <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Prior to Guns N' Roses' appearance, Metallica's set was cut short after singer-guitarist <a href="/wiki/James_Hetfield" title="James Hetfield">James Hetfield</a> suffered second-degree burns in a pyrotechnics accident. However, Guns N' Roses was unable to go on stage early, because Rose once again was late arriving at the venue. Nearly an hour into their show, Rose complained of voice problems before walking off stage, following which a riot erupted in downtown Montreal, resulting in an estimated $400,000 in damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spitz99_39-7"><a href="#cite_note-Spitz99-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In November of that year, Rose was convicted of property damage and assault in relation to the Riverport riot; he was fined $50,000 and received two years' probation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kent03_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kent03-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Guns N' Roses played its final show of the Use Your Illusion Tour on July 17, 1993 at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Plate_Stadium" title="River Plate Stadium">River Plate Stadium</a> in Buenos Aires;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> it proved to be Rose's last live performance with the band for seven and a half years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClassicRock03_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-ClassicRock03-57">[57]</a></sup> The following August, Rose testified in court against Steven Adler, who had filed a lawsuit contending that he had been illegitimately fired. When the judge ruled against Rose, he agreed to an out-of-court settlement of $2,500,000 and 15% of the royalties for everything Adler recorded prior to his departure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wall07_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wall07-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kent03_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kent03-47">[47]</a></sup> In November of that year, Guns N' Roses released <i><a href="/wiki/%22The_Spaghetti_Incident%3F%22" title='"The Spaghetti Incident?"'>"The Spaghetti Incident?"</a></i> a cover album of mostly punk songs, which proved less successful than its predecessors. Rose had included the hidden track "<a href="/wiki/Look_at_Your_Game,_Girl" title="Look at Your Game, Girl">Look at Your Game, Girl</a>", a song written by convicted murderer <a href="/wiki/Charles_Manson" title="Charles Manson">Charles Manson</a>, which he intended as a personal message to his ex-girlfriend <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Seymour" title="Stephanie Seymour">Stephanie Seymour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kent03_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kent03-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stickwith_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stickwith-59">[59]</a></sup> Controversy ensued, and the band subsequently pledged to donate any royalties to the son of one of Manson's victims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wall07_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wall07-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manson_cover_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manson_cover-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1994.E2.80.932000:_Hiatus">1994–2000: Hiatus</span></h3>
<p>Without consultation from his band mates, Rose did not renew Gilby Clarke's contract with the band in June 1994,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wall07_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-Wall07-17">[17]</a></sup> as he claimed Clarke to be only a "hired hand."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Tension between Rose and Slash reached a breaking point after the latter discovered that Rose had hired his childhood friend <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tobias" title="Paul Tobias">Paul "Huge" Tobias</a> as Clarke's replacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wall07_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-Wall07-17">[17]</a></sup> Although the band recorded material during this time, it was ultimately not used because, according to Rose, their lack of collaboration prevented them from producing their best work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Slash finally left Guns N' Roses in October 1996 due to his differences with Rose,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> while Matt Sorum was fired in June 1997 after an argument over Tobias's involvement in the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Duff McKagan departed the band in August of that year, leaving Rose and Dizzy Reed as the only remaining band members of the <i>Use Your Illusion</i> era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStone00_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStone00-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the stability of Guns N' Roses collapsed, Rose withdrew from public view. The band never officially broke up, although it did not tour or perform for several years and no new material was released. Rose continued to recruit new musicians to replace band members who either left or were fired. By the late 1990s, he was considered to be a recluse, rarely making public appearances and spending most of his time in his mansion in <a href="/wiki/Malibu,_California" title="Malibu, California">Malibu</a>. In various media reports, he was referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes" title="Howard Hughes">Howard Hughes</a> of rock" and "rock's greatest recluse."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spitz99_39-8"><a href="#cite_note-Spitz99-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sutcliffe01_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sutcliffe01-65">[65]</a></sup> Rose was said to spend his nights rehearsing and writing with the various new lineups of Guns N' Roses, working on the band's next album, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Democracy_(album)" title="Chinese Democracy (album)">Chinese Democracy</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStone00_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStone00-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2001.E2.80.9311:_Touring_in_support_of_Chinese_Democracy">2001–11: Touring in support of <i>Chinese Democracy</i></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AxlRose_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="220" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/AxlRose_cropped.jpg/170px-AxlRose_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d1/AxlRose_cropped.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AxlRose_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rose at the <a href="/wiki/Download_Festival" title="Download Festival">Download Festival</a> in Donington Park, England, in June 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In January 2001, Rose resurfaced with Guns N' Roses at <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio#Rock_in_Rio_3" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio 3</a> to commence the decade-long <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Democracy_Tour" title="Chinese Democracy Tour">Chinese Democracy Tour</a>, though the majority of its scheduled concerts over the next two years did not take place. A critically panned surprise appearance at the <a href="/wiki/2002_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2002 MTV Video Music Awards">2002 MTV Video Music Awards</a> was followed by an incident in November when a riot erupted at Vancouver's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Motors_Place" title="General Motors Place">General Motors Place</a> after Rose failed to show up for a scheduled concert. When venue staff announced the cancellation, a riot broke out, resulting in an estimated $100,000 in damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClassicRock03_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-ClassicRock03-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> As the band's line-up continued to evolve, his constant band mates were guitarist <a href="/wiki/Richard_Fortus" title="Richard Fortus">Richard Fortus</a>, bassist <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Stinson" title="Tommy Stinson">Tommy Stinson</a>, and keyboardists Dizzy Reed and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Pitman" title="Chris Pitman">Chris Pitman</a>.</p>
<p>After the tour was cancelled by the promoter, Rose again withdrew from the public view. During this time, he joined Slash and Duff McKagan in a lawsuit against Geffen Records in an unsuccessful attempt to block the release of the <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Guns_N%27_Roses_album)" title="Greatest Hits (Guns N' Roses album)">Greatest Hits</a></i> compilation album,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> and lent his voice to the 2004 video game <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto:_San_Andreas" title="Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas">Grand Theft Auto: San Andreas</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In a rare interview in January 2006, Rose stated that "people will hear music this year."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> While Guns N' Roses toured extensively throughout 2006 and 2007, with several guest appearances by Izzy Stradlin, <i>Chinese Democracy</i> again failed to materialize.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Rose did collaborate with his friend <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Bach" title="Sebastian Bach">Sebastian Bach</a> on his album <i><a href="/wiki/Angel_Down" title="Angel Down">Angel Down</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fifteen years after its last album, in November 2008, Guns N' Roses released <i>Chinese Democracy</i> exclusively via the electronics retailer <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Rose did not contribute to the album's promotion; by December, he had reportedly been missing for at least two months and had not returned phone calls or other requests from his record label.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> In a subsequent interview, Rose stated that he felt he had not received the necessary support from <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> A year after the album's release, in December 2009, Guns N' Roses embarked on another two-and-a-half years of touring, including a headlining performance at <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio#Rock_in_Rio_4" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio 4</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Rose was subsequently sued by former band manager <a href="/wiki/Irving_Azoff" title="Irving Azoff">Irving Azoff</a>, who sought $1.87 million in unpaid fees related to the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-azoff_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-azoff-78">[78]</a></sup> In a countersuit, Rose alleged Azoff had deliberately mismanaged the band and their album's promotion to force him to join his former band mates for a reunion tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWsuit_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-EWsuit-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Both cases were settled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> According to Rose in 2011, part of the settlement agreement dictated that Rose and the current Guns N' Roses had to do a number of performances with Azoff's company <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_Nation" title="Live Nation">Live Nation</a> as the promoter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2010, Rose sued <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>, the producers of the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero" title="Guitar Hero">Guitar Hero</a></i>, for $20 million, claiming that Activision had violated an agreement with him to not include any reference to Slash or his band <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolver" title="Velvet Revolver">Velvet Revolver</a> in the game in return for a license to use the song "<a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_the_Jungle" title="Welcome to the Jungle">Welcome to the Jungle</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-THR-84">[84]</a></sup> Instead, Rose noted that an image of Slash was used on the game's front cover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-THR-84">[84]</a></sup> Rose's claim was summarily dismissed in February 2013, when the judge ruled that Rose had not brought suit on the contract, which relied on oral promises, within the two-year <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_limitations" title="Statute of limitations">statute of limitations</a> that began with the game's October 2007 release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-THR-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.E2.80.93present:_Hall_of_Fame_and_regrouping.3B_AC.2FDC">2012–present: Hall of Fame and regrouping; AC/DC</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ACDC_with_AxlRose_WashingtonDC_17-SEP-2016.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1594" data-file-width="1889" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/ACDC_with_AxlRose_WashingtonDC_17-SEP-2016.jpg/220px-ACDC_with_AxlRose_WashingtonDC_17-SEP-2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/ACDC_with_AxlRose_WashingtonDC_17-SEP-2016.jpg/330px-ACDC_with_AxlRose_WashingtonDC_17-SEP-2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/ACDC_with_AxlRose_WashingtonDC_17-SEP-2016.jpg/440px-ACDC_with_AxlRose_WashingtonDC_17-SEP-2016.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ACDC_with_AxlRose_WashingtonDC_17-SEP-2016.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rose performing with <a href="/wiki/AC/DC" title="AC/DC">AC/DC</a> in 2016.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Together with the other members of Guns N' Roses' classic lineup, Rose was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 2012, their first year of eligibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> He did not attend the induction ceremony in April, however,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> as he had announced in an open letter three days prior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-87">[87]</a></sup> Rose, who had long been on bad terms with several of his former band mates, wrote that the ceremony "doesn't appear to be somewhere I'm actually wanted or respected."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-87">[87]</a></sup> He subsequently joined his band in <a href="/wiki/Artist-in-residence" title="Artist-in-residence">residencies</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Joint_(music_venue)" title="The Joint (music venue)">The Joint</a> in Las Vegas in 2012 and 2014, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Appetite_for_Democracy_(Tour)" title="Appetite for Democracy (Tour)">Appetite for Democracy Tour</a> celebrating the anniversaries of <i>Appetite for Destruction</i> and <i>Chinese Democracy</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> By mid-2014, the group's new album, recorded concurrently with <i>Chinese Democracy</i>, and a remix album were completed and pending release, but no new material emerged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>In response to an informal study that named him the 'World's Greatest Singer" based on a study of vocal ranges, Rose told <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> in 2014, "If I had to say who I thought the best singers were, I'd say first that I don't know there's a definitive answer as in my opinion it's subjective, and second that my focus is primarily rock singers. That said, I enjoy <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_McCafferty" title="Dan McCafferty">Dan McCafferty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janis_Joplin" title="Janis Joplin">Janis Joplin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Daltrey" title="Roger Daltrey">Roger Daltrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Henley" title="Don Henley">Don Henley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Lynne" title="Jeff Lynne">Jeff Lynne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash" title="Johnny Cash">Johnny Cash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Scott" title="Jimmy Scott">Jimmy Scott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etta_James" title="Etta James">Etta James</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiona_Apple" title="Fiona Apple">Fiona Apple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chrissie_Hynde" title="Chrissie Hynde">Chrissie Hynde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Brown" title="James Brown">James Brown</a> and a ton of others (predominantly Seventies rock singers) and would rather hear any of them anytime rather than me!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rose and Slash reunited for the <a href="/wiki/Not_in_This_Lifetime..._Tour" title="Not in This Lifetime... Tour">Not in This Lifetime... Tour</a>, one of the most-anticipated reunion tours in rock history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greene16_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greene16-92">[92]</a></sup> Alongside Dizzy Reed and returning member Duff McKagan, who had previously made guest appearances with the band, they comprised two-thirds of the band's <i>Use Your Illusion</i>-era line-up, with <i>Chinese Democracy</i>-era members <a href="/wiki/Richard_Fortus" title="Richard Fortus">Richard Fortus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ferrer" title="Frank Ferrer">Frank Ferrer</a> joining new member <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Reese" title="Melissa Reese">Melissa Reese</a> to fill out the rest of the lineup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Rose shared a stage with Slash for the first time in nearly 23 years during the group's surprise performance at The Troubadour in April 2016, ahead of its headlining shows at <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greene16_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-Greene16-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> He additionally joined Australian hard rock band <a href="/wiki/AC/DC" title="AC/DC">AC/DC</a> to perform as lead singer for the remainder of the band's <a href="/wiki/Rock_or_Bust_World_Tour" title="Rock or Bust World Tour">Rock or Bust World Tour</a>, after long-time lead vocalist <a href="/wiki/Brian_Johnson" title="Brian Johnson">Brian Johnson</a> had to stop touring due to hearing problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS_April_2016_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-RS_April_2016-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Axl_Rose_Nottingham_2012.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1023" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Axl_Rose_Nottingham_2012.JPG/220px-Axl_Rose_Nottingham_2012.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Axl_Rose_Nottingham_2012.JPG/330px-Axl_Rose_Nottingham_2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Axl_Rose_Nottingham_2012.JPG/440px-Axl_Rose_Nottingham_2012.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Axl_Rose_Nottingham_2012.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rose performing "<a href="/wiki/November_Rain" title="November Rain">November Rain</a>" at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nottingham_Arena" title="Nottingham Arena">Nottingham Arena</a> in Nottingham, England, in May 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_issues">Health issues</span></h3>
<p>During Rose's late teens, a psychiatrist concluded that his delinquent behavior was evidence of <a href="/wiki/Psychosis" title="Psychosis">psychosis</a>. In addition, he made note of his high IQ.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tannenbaum88_15-6"><a href="#cite_note-Tannenbaum88-15">[15]</a></sup> In a subsequent interview, he questioned the diagnosis altogether, stating, "I went to a clinic, thinking it would help my moods. The only thing I did was take one 500-question test—ya know, filling in the little black dots. All of sudden I'm diagnosed manic-depressive. 'Let's put Axl on medication.' Well, the medication doesn't help me deal with stress. The only thing it does is help keep people off my back because they figure I'm on medication."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIPJames89_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIPJames89-97">[97]</a></sup> In contrast to his public image, Rose was not a heavy drug user, though he did not disavow the use of illicit substances entirely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kent03_47-4"><a href="#cite_note-Kent03-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIPJames89_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-RIPJames89-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the early 1990s, Rose became a staunch believer in homeopathic medicine, and began regularly undergoing <a href="/wiki/Past_life_regression" title="Past life regression">past life regression</a> therapy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStone00_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStone00-16">[16]</a></sup> He went public with his "uncovered memories" of being sexually abused by his biological father at the age of two,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStoneBio_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStoneBio-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely92_18-8"><a href="#cite_note-Neely92-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sischy92_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sischy92-43">[43]</a></sup> which he said had stunted his emotional growth: "When they talk about Axl Rose being a screaming two-year-old, they're right."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neely92_18-9"><a href="#cite_note-Neely92-18">[18]</a></sup> His dislike of touring was caused in part by the various illnesses he contracted over time. He expressed his belief that these health problems were caused by him unconsciously lowering his own resistance as a form of "self-punishment".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="With_Rapidfire">With Rapidfire</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i>Ready to Rumble</i> (2014)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guest_appearances">Guest appearances</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Decline_of_Western_Civilization_Part_II:_The_Metal_Years" title="The Decline of Western Civilization Part II: The Metal Years">The Decline of Western Civilization Part II: The Metal Years – Original Motion Picture Soundtrack</a></i> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Various_artists" title="Various artists">various artists</a> (1988; "<a href="/wiki/Under_My_Wheels" title="Under My Wheels">Under My Wheels</a>" ft. <a href="/wiki/Alice_Cooper" title="Alice Cooper">Alice Cooper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slash_(musician)" title="Slash (musician)">Slash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Izzy_Stradlin" title="Izzy Stradlin">Izzy Stradlin</a>)</li>
